The Umpire before the snap is 15 yards behind the line of scrimmage.  Dak Prescott runs for a 17 yard gain.   That's 32 yards of space created by Dak Prescott for the Umpire to travel to get to the spot.  The Umpire didn't do this.  Dak Prescott did it on his own.   It's not a question of the Umpire being late.  The Umpire gets there when he gets there.  Dak Prescott created too much space and distance.  He gets an F for situational awareness.    Then Dak Prescott and the Dallas Offensive Line build a wall between the Umpire and the football.  NFL Rule 3, Article 2, Section 2 is unambiguous.  "A Dead Ball is Ready for Play while the 40-second Play Clock is running when the ball is placed down by an official at the spot where the ball will next be put in play, or when the Referee signals for the 25-second Play Clock to start."  Instead of making it easy for the Umpire to place the ball down at the spot, Dak Prescott and the Dallas Offensive Line hinder him, not once but twice.   Dak Prescott and the Dallas Offensive get an F for situational awareness.  The Umpire did his job and followed the rules.
